Patriotic Goods Speech

Record of Mr. Chen Diaofu's Speech 207

— Lü Bin

—Manager of Yongli Chemical Industry Company—

After the September 18th National Crisis, the Ministry of Industry once drafted a plan to establish a large-scale sulfuric acid factory for manufacturing fertilizer to develop national industry, resist foreign goods, and reduce leakage. At that time, because of China's economic shortfalls, there was not so much capital to start. So, it was prepared to jointly run with the UK and Germany, using their capital to develop our local business. Experts from the UK and Germany were invited to design together with our country's industrial experts. Mr. Chen Diaofu was also one of them. Later, the UK and Germany had no sincerity. They thought that if they helped China develop this kind of business, it would affect the sales of their foreign goods in China. Therefore, they wanted to manipulate and control it, wanting to grab this kind of business in their hands and not let China have sovereignty. Their long-standing intention to invade can be imagined. Therefore, Mr. Chen Diaofu believed that state-owned enterprises must not be controlled by foreigners. If so, wouldn't it be giving foreigners further aggression? So, he asked the Ministry of Industry to start it independently. The Ministry of Industry, due to financial difficulties, asked Mr. Chen's Yongli Chemical Industry Company to handle it. Mr. Chen tried to negotiate with the Shanghai banking community, and got the approval of the banking community. So, it was decided to use domestic capital to set up a sulfuric acid manufacturing plant in Xiejiatian, located between Liuhe County and Pukou on the north bank of the Yangtze River. Now, preparations have been completed and are actively underway, and it will soon be started.

Mr. Chen enjoys a great reputation in the domestic goods industry in the country. For the worker education problem in the factory, he went to Wuxi the day before yesterday to visit Mr. Gao Jiansi, the president of the Education Institute, to discuss how to run labor education in the factory, and took the opportunity to give a speech. We were able to see his demeanor and hear him talk about important information about Yongli Chemical Industry Company.

Mr. Chen said that the alkali plant he ran in Tanggu, Tianjin, has been more than ten years. It manufactures three kinds of pure alkali (sodium carbonate), caustic soda (sodium hydroxide), and clean alkali (sodium bicarbonate). Bread, fried dough sticks, papermaking, glasses, dyeing, etc., all need alkali. The domestic consumption alone is a large number. In the past, they were all purchased from the British Imperial Chemical Industries Company, and there were many losses every year. After their alkali manufacturing company was established, they resisted British goods. The alkali materials used in the country are all their products. Not only are they sold in the domestic market, but they are also transported to Japan. Japan's alkali manufacturing industry is not as good as China's. It is estimated that they can recover 5 million yuan of rights and interests every year.

He also said that his purpose of running this kind of industry is not for personal gain, but to focus on national industry, to serve the domestic goods industry, in order to develop the domestic national capital industry. He said that all the products of their alkali manufacturing company have a position in the world. It is the glory of the Chinese domestic goods industry, not personal glory. If it is based on personal interests to start a business, there is really not much meaning. These words are extremely thorough! The reason why our Chinese domestic goods business cannot develop is because of short-sightedness, unable to focus on the big picture, only seeking personal gain.

He also said that to manufacture domestic goods, we must use domestic raw materials. For example, the most important raw material for manufacturing sulfuric acid is sulfur. According to his investigation, Hunan has the most sulfur production. So, he also planned how to develop Hunan's sulfur mines.

Finally, he talked about that in addition to the existing alkali manufacturing company and the sulfuric acid plant under construction, Yongli Chemical Industry Company will also run a ammonia plant, manufacturing ammonia: an acid plant, manufacturing sulfuric acid, nitric acid. Because the need for these raw materials to manufacture many goods are large in quantity. If we do not actively do it ourselves, money will flow out every day. If this continues, there will never be a time to save it.

New Domestic Goods Information in a Week

Japanese merchants are now actively restoring trade with China, and Japanese ships that have been suspended for more than three years have also resumed their routes one after another.

The Capital Spring Domestic Goods Exhibition will be held on May 1st, and is now collecting domestic goods from various factories to participate.

Chen Jitang proposed in the provincial government to prohibit civil servants from wearing foreign clothes.

The Yunnan Provincial Domestic Goods Exhibition was held in Kunming on April 1st. Mrs. Long Yun unveiled it. 50,000 to 60,000 people participated, and domestic goods were sold out.

China National Goods Company and International Wireless Radio jointly organize children's broadcasts.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 208

— (Cheng Zhenru)

Silkworm moths are sexually promiscuous. Since they crawl out of the cocoon, they flutter their wings to find the opposite sex. Suddenly mating and laying eggs, the male dies first after mating, and the female also dies after laying eggs. You see its short life of one or twenty hours after becoming a moth, as if it is only for sexual intercourse and laying eggs.

Isn't life a hundred years just a moment? Instead of taking advantage of this precious time to work hard on a vigorous career that benefits the country and the people, and focusing on "abundant offspring" and "continuous melons and silkworms," waiting for woe is me, this kind of life meaning is like a reproductive machine, and what is the difference with a sexually promiscuous silkworm moth?

Although the words are said like this, in the vast universe, how many people can escape this kind of silkworm moth-like life?

Hilsa Herring Talk 209

— Shijiu

The Hilsa herring, hated by Su Dongpo for being "bony," is now on the market. Hilsa herring from the Fuchun River are the best. Everyone knows this, it seems unnecessary to say more; but why the Hilsa herring from the Fuchun River can be famous and renowned, there is still a small anecdote in the middle, which is described as follows:

Hilsa herring are originally sea creatures, but every spring, they must go to freshwater rivers and swim for a long time. It is said that their biggest purpose is to spawn. Therefore, once the spring river warms up, they all abandon their old homes; it seems that they cannot get used to that sea life, and they must move to a better place and swim into the river to live.

There is a Zhizi Gate—commonly known as Zhizi Gate—in the Qiantang River—mountain peaks stand on both sides, and when the tide reaches there, it is blocked, and there is a view of surging rocks and shallow waters, so that place is the best place to watch the tide in August. When scaly fish arrive at Zhizi Gate, probably due to lack of strength, or because they love the surging tide there, they lie in the river to spawn, completing their task of passing on the species.

After the task is completed, they go up the river. When they arrive at the Fuchun River, they are living leisurely and contentedly. Unexpectedly, there is a generation of people who like to feast, because those mother fish are weak after production and easy to catch, they wait for the opportunity, and a seasonal fresh product is added to the knife board. The Hilsa herring caught at this time is the freshest and most expensive, not something poor scholars can afford. If they luckily escape the net, go upstream, and then go downstream, and are caught again, their meat will be old, and they will not be valued.

The above was described by a Fuyang friend, so I recorded it.

Tennis 210

— Chonglou

People who grew up in old families are mostly weak.

In the past year, in the letters I wrote home, I always advised my older brother and sister to pay attention to exercise and strengthen their bodies. —

Perhaps these words will touch their hearts after a long time. Recently, I received a letter from my younger sister, saying that they are already preparing to set up a family tennis court.

Hearing that they want to implement fitness, I feel very happy in my heart; but I know that sports equipment in my hometown is inferior and expensive, so I spent half a day selecting four rackets, a net, and two dozen balls for them, and sent them back by mail.

At the same time, in the letter I sent to them, in addition to roughly stating some opinions on the setting of the court and the method of practice, I also wrote to them: "...With a healthy body, you can have a lively spirit. ...Health is really priceless! For it, don't be stingy with some time!..."

Indeed, among all sports, tennis is more interesting; and it has an average development for wrist strength, foot strength, eyesight, and various parts of the body. When I was in school, I was a "tennis fan"; but now because of the busyness of work, I rarely have the opportunity to play it. Although there is a new court in my hometown family now, I am far away in another country, and I can't help but feel a little sad!

The Colors of the Country 211

— (Wu Ershui)

There are several countries in the world now, like the maps published in bookstores, dyed in various different colors. Now writing him down is a strange picture!

The Soviet Union is "red."

The Russians who came out of exile are "white." —commonly called him "White Russian."

Italy is "black." That was dyed after the black-clothed prime minister came to power.

Germany is "brown." This is "born" at the same time as Hitler.

The United States is shrouded in a "blue" color. This came with the restoration movement.

Sir Mosley of England is trying to turn England "black" again.

Red, white, black, brown, blue, it can really be said to be "colorful."

Rejuvenation Doctor 213

— (Ji Yun)

Frenchman Shan Luoqiu is the director of the French Experimental Surgical Research Institute, and has the secret method of rejuvenation, which is famous in Europe and America. Recently, he took his 21-year-old wife on a honeymoon trip to Japan. Staying in the Imperial Hotel, three rooms with 50 yuan a day were opened, and the behavior was extravagant, so the Japanese paid close attention to him.

Dr. Jia is very rich, and the couple lives in Colimtai City on the border between Italy and France. Many gorillas and apes are kept at home for research. They live in the countryside in summer and move to Paris in winter. There are five cars for moving. The doctor is 65 years old this year. Although his hair is slightly white, he still looks like a young man. In terms of age, his beautiful and young wife can only be his granddaughter. According to the doctor, the method of rejuvenation is like grafting a sweet persimmon branch onto an astringent persimmon tree, and then you can grow sweet persimmons. Implanting the testicles of gorillas or apes on the human body can rejuvenate, but the method is not as simple as grafting trees. A reporter asked if his wife had had surgery. The doctor replied that she was only twenty-one years old, and if she had surgery, she would not be able to bear children.

The doctor claimed that he had never tried the rejuvenation surgery himself. But he has used surgery on his younger brother, and he has indeed rejuvenated for ten years. It is said that surgery can be used about once every ten years.

Records of Imperial Incense Floating 214

— Originally written by Princess Qingdeling, translated by Qin Shouou

I remember that the first time I followed the Empress Dowager, the Empress Dowager also talked to me in detail. "It may surprise you! Every time we make a pair of shoes, from the beginning of the sample to the complete completion, it must take at least a month." The Empress Dowager first said to me, "This is really a very troublesome project, and there are indeed many procedures involved! Even these girls, you can't underestimate them! Their skills are extremely skilled, and the workers outside can't compare to them!...First, they always have to draw a shoe pattern on white paper: drawing a shoe pattern is a very thoughtful project, and all aspects must be taken care of. Such as shoe material style, pattern, etc..., nothing must be properly considered and configured in order to be appropriate; and among them, the height of the heel should be determined first..."

Then, she and I specifically discussed the heel. —The heel here refers specifically to the high-heeled shoes worn by women in Manchuria at the beginning. (This kind of high-heeled shoes is commonly called flag shoes. Their style is similar to the high-heeled shoes worn by women in Middle Earth, except that the head is not pointed, and a wooden heel is installed under the sole. But the position of this wooden heel is not on the heel at the back, but in the middle of the sole; people wearing this kind of high-heeled shoes walk, it is really like stepping on a pair of low stilts, with a unique flowing posture.) —The height of this kind of heel must correspond to the thickness of the sole above and the style of the shoes; a certain kind of sole must be matched with a certain size of wooden heel, which must be carefully studied, otherwise the wearer will feel uncomfortable, and even feel pain. (290)

Whereabouts

A Trip to Longhua 215

— Wu Huanbing

On Sunday afternoon, I was dismissed from duty at just the right time—four o'clock. My heart, weighed down by the pressures of my environment, sluggish and devoid of the excitement a young person should have, received a bit of a baptism in the warm sunlight, and surprisingly, I felt a stirring of life. Dragging my leaden feet, I wandered aimlessly forward. Before I knew it, I was in the old western district. Every shop doorway was filled with the sounds of music, and the sidewalks were crowded with people coming and going, a scene of peaceful prosperity.

I had just stopped when a shiny, new public bus, freshly painted by the municipal public utility bureau and specifically for the Longhua line, pulled up. A large group of people poured out of the bus, most of them holding a bunch of peach blossoms in their hands, the petals falling off with a rustling sound from the jostling—how cruel, I thought. Then another large group boarded the bus. I called out to two younger colleagues, "We have nothing to do anyway, let's go have some fun!"

The bus drove smoothly on the road, the gravel road, the cinder road, passing Gaochang Temple, Nanyang Middle School, and Xiaomu Bridge. All along the way were rural scenes. The golden rapeseed flowers were so lovely. A small stream meandered in front of us, winding and turning, and I wondered where it led. Across the stream was a magnificent vista of spring. "One willow, one peach," the ancient poem perfectly captured the scene. Behind the dense layers of peach and willow trees, stood a delicate pagoda, sadly worn and dilapidated with age, but all the more ancient and quaint for it.

We had arrived at Longhua, our destination. Everyone got off the bus. Sure enough, there were many tourists: old ladies with yellow cloth bags, devoutly burning incense; fashionable gentlemen and ladies out for a stroll; groups of mischievous elementary school students; and some, bored and hoping to find a bit of inspiration and comfort. We walked into the main gate of the ancient temple, where vendors were hawking their wares on the incense and candle stands. In front of the main hall, a lay Buddhist of unknown name was gesticulating and expounding the scriptures, surrounded by a large crowd of devout men and women listening intently. The Three Buddhas in the Hall of the Great Hero were being gilded, and the five hundred majestic statues in the Hall of Arhats were solemn, reverent, inspiring spontaneous respect.

The buildings around the main hall had been renovated. Although they were simple, they were a complete change from the dilapidated state of the past. We walked around the temple once and then left.

Outside the temple gate, it wasn't far to the airfield via the railway station. In this vast open space, at twilight, I walked along, imagining the sound of airplanes rumbling overhead, our brave soldiers skillfully flying light fighter planes in neat formations, singing the stirring anthem "Return Our Glorious Rivers and Mountains," a triumphant song filled with fervor.

The scenery of the Southern Huangpu was beautiful. The white sails of boats moved across the water. The shadows of the three of us stood on the beach, listening to the sound of the river tide crashing in the wind. Infinite thoughts surged in our hearts, and the curtain of night was closing in around us!

Little Xitian 216

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 11: A Sad Conversation Reveals That Life is But a Dream; Random Footprints Show How Cruel the Wind and Rain Are

Zhiqian thought to himself, matchmaking isn't like putting out a fire, so why are these two women struggling so desperately in the rain, coming and going? There must be something wrong. Since it's raining anyway, and I can't meet with friends, I'm going to stay by the window and see what's going on. Thinking this, he stayed in the room, never leaving the window. Sure enough, less than half an hour later, three women arrived. Leading the way were Sister-in-law Hu and the woman who had left earlier, sharing an umbrella. Behind them was the young girl Zhu Yueying, holding her own umbrella. As Sister-in-law Hu walked, she kept talking. Behind the glass, her words were unclear, but Yueying seemed to be responding constantly. It seemed she was directing her to do something. Zhiqian thought that in the oblique wind and drizzle, they were hurriedly making contact, definitely to bring Yueying here. Could it be that someone wants to take her away from Xi'an? But Xi'an is a place where you can only travel by land, and when it rains, sedans, cars, and mules can't move. Why the rush? Besides, what other reason would there be for such a hurry? Unable to figure it out, Zhiqian refused to let go. He immediately ran out of the room and stood under the veranda. They were in the courtyard, following the brick path around the corner of the house, just coming over. (179)

Finance: Gold Market—Balanced Supply and Demand, Zhu Tupan's Actions—A Yuan Lost 217

Yesterday, the gold market saw overseas silver markets rising across the board. The morning opened with further declines, but market sentiment was still good. The foreign exchange market, which had been tight, eased, and the overdrafts continued to dry up, making a rebound easy. Trading in the morning remained inactive, with supply and demand very average and prices fluctuating without direction, resulting in a slight decline. At the start of the morning, overseas silver markets in both the UK and US were up, but there was talk of a seller hanging a price of 0.0625 lower than the posted price after the close. Silver for forward delivery in Montreaux rose sharply. Foreign exchange rates rose slightly, London spot gold fell 9.5 pence, and off-exchange forward trading fell to 63.75 yuan. Buyers became active at lower prices, and prices rose accordingly. The Central Bank's posted rate was announced, with the pound unchanged and the US dollar up 0.0625. The customs gold unit fell by one cent, and the gold standard fell to 900.4 yuan. The morning opened on a low note, with Jewish merchants Qiao Zhinan actively buying. The domestic US dollar market gradually tightened, and buyers surged in after the opening, causing prices to rise. However, because banks took the opportunity to sell at high prices, the rise was temporary, and prices fell back. Upon learning that the HSBC posted rate was unchanged for the pound and up 0.0625 for the US dollar, there was some fluctuation, but after the Central Bank showed willingness to sell US dollars, and the Bank of Japan also divested, prices once fell. However, banks seized the opportunity to buy at lower prices, and buyers were also active at the lower levels. Soon, prices rose again. Although Sassoon suddenly showed a desire to sell, causing a temporary decline, the banks' appetite remained strong. There were not many transactions in the market, and short positions were covered, keeping the overall trend stable. Finally, the price rose slightly because the Bank of China intended to cover US dollars, and the market closed steady. Trading in the morning was initially weak but strengthened later, with tight positions, but the continued weakness in forward contracts made it difficult for market sentiment to improve, and the market remained dull. The morning's market activity is recorded below:

The morning opened at 865.3 yuan, down 1.8 yuan from the previous close. Huixiang, Fuyu, Dadecheng, Hengyu, Yingxiang, Yuanheng and others came. Hengyu and Fuxing Yong sold contracts, and with uncertain sentiment, the price fell to 5 yuan. Jinlong, Yingxiang, Yuanmao, Yongchang, and Da Shang Na rose to 6.4 yuan. Upon learning that the HSBC posted rate was unchanged for the pound and up 0.0625 for the US dollar, the situation stabilized. The Central Bank suddenly offered 43,750 US dollars for July delivery, and Wanxing Dafa Yonghengyu sold to 4 yuan, with a profit on the June sterling at 625. Yingxiang Hengchang Yongjin rose to 5.2 yuan, and Hengyu, Dadecheng, Changda and others sold contracts in succession. Mitsui also sold June sterling at 25, falling to 3.5 yuan. Yuqing Yongfu and Yong Wanxing Hengyu Hanheng Yuanmao Yongheng Changyong Jinlong Dafa Yong all bought, gradually rising back to 6.6 yuan. Sassoon suddenly showed a real intention to sell, and Huixiang Yuanchang Yonghengyu Dadecheng Fuyu took the opportunity to sell at high prices, retreating to 4.2 yuan. Fuyu Yicheng Shunmao Yuqing Yongjin Longlai entered the market, and prices rose again to 7.5 yuan. Sassoon offered April sterling at 75, and Lifeng Yu Yingxiang sold, falling back to 4.9 yuan. Zhengjin bought May US dollars at 6875, and Richang Fuxing Yongda Fengzhengchang Shunzang Yongli and others maintained prices. There was talk of China's intention to buy April US dollars at 125, rising to 6.9 yuan. Dafa Yong and others supplied at high prices, and the midday close was 866.1 yuan. After the close, prices were flat, hovering around 6 yuan. The highest price for the morning was 868 yuan, and the lowest price was 863.5 yuan, with a fluctuation of 4.5 yuan. As a result, the price fell 1 yuan compared to the previous close.

The closing price, according to the Central Bank's gold standard price, was 900.4 yuan, approximately 34 yuan below the closing price, a decrease of about 4 yuan from the previous close. The discount price for this month was 863 yuan, and for May it was 866 yuan. The morning discount was 863 yuan, and red gold bonds were priced about 4 yuan higher, at 869.3 yuan. The spot market was calm, with Tianjin goods priced about 7 yuan higher. Only 119 contracts remained for this month, mostly held by Dafang Tongfeng Heng Gan Changxiang Qingfa Yongrun Changyu Juchang Dafeng Hengrun Changshui Jiarun eight firms, and shorted by Shenkang and Dingtai two firms.

Trading in the market was average. Dadecheng Yiyu Dachangxiang Fuyu Yuanchang Yongfu Xingyong Yuyuan Yongheng Yongdesheng Datong Taichang Dafa Yong Lifeng Shunli Shenkang and others were mostly sellers, while Huixiang Yuqing Yongyu Xinxiang Shunmao Yingxiang Hongkang Yongren Fa Yongyi Fengyong Jinlong Manheng Yuansheng Yong Hongxing Yongfeng and others were mostly buyers. Both morning and afternoon trading sessions in the flour market saw steady gains. Speculators, citing unfavorable weather conditions, refrained from selling, and active trading by speculators further drove up prices. As a result, prices for April and May rose by a half, June by 1.25, and September by 1.0.

According to reports from Hankou, black tea from Hunan and Hubei provinces has suddenly become active recently. Tea merchants are very enthusiastic due to the sharp increase in sales to British plantations compared to previous years. Recently, 107 tea processing factories in Anhua, Taoyuan, Changshou Street, Niejiashi, and Yang Er and other places are preparing to open. Banks in Hankou have also issued loans totaling over 3 million yuan. The lively situation is vastly different from previous years. According to estimates from general tea merchants, the future production of black tea in Hunan and Hubei may exceed 200,000 boxes.

Casually Thinking of Oblomov 233

— Leng Mo

I've always heard that Oblomov is written as a character worthy of ridicule, but when reading it, it's hard to see that the author intended to write Oblomov as a laughable figure. It seems to be the opposite; the author, through the mouth of Olga, praises him in the end as the purest and most virtuous person in the world, and this is said very earnestly. Certainly, Goncharov was a proponent of Westernization; he felt that the old Russian way of life could no longer be maintained. He sang the paean for Westernization and tolled the death knell for Oblomov. But death does not seem to be something to be mocked, and thus the author’s pen also does not flow with an air of mockery. The author seems very optimistic and is not worried that someone will continue to live the life of Oblomov. Originally, that kind of person could not be like Don Quixote, firmly embracing the vanished past. They disappeared without a trace along with the past, or perhaps because their disappearance was so bleak, it made one feel sad along with them, and their purity and goodness became something that could not be missed with sincerity.

If Oblomov had not encountered the decline of his family, if he had not only had some land left, but could still have been a major landowner, relying on a good steward on his estate, and had a peaceful life, he would have been the best of his kind. However, although he grew up in such an environment, he could not continue peacefully. He could only entrust his few properties to someone else to manage and throw himself into an unfamiliar society. The person he entrusted cheated him, and the first people he met also cheated him. His servants, like him, were ignorant of the world and encouraged him to maintain the old way of life. There is no doubt that such an environment could not encourage his advancement, so he, at most, only maintained his simplicity.

He met Olga too late, and Olga was also a simple person like him. She did not have the ability to transform his life. In love, it cannot be denied that Oblomov dominated her because she was deeply moved by his character and loved him. The Oblomov that the author wrote about in love is indeed extremely lovable. Perhaps this is why Chekhov ridiculed Goncharov as vulgar. The author is fully using the methods of writing an ideal romance. However, if we do not preconceive what Oblomov should be written as, then the role that Oblomov plays in the romance is not bad. He did not hide his weaknesses and force himself to be a hero. His weaknesses led to the failure of his love in the end. He was willing to simply think that this was the result of his own weakness, and he acknowledged that for Olga's happiness, he should be abandoned. In this way, all the weaknesses still completely filled his lovableness.

Given that he was loved by Olga and loved by the landlord, it is naturally not surprising. Because this is a relatively vulgar romance, the result is marriage, ordinarily until his death. This ending does not seem to change Oblomov's character, so in this respect, he is not particularly reprehensible. I am naturally not trying to forcefully say his advantages here and thus excuse his weariness. I only want to say that since Goncharov tried his best to write his advantages, then the impression he wanted to give us may not be entirely the same as what I have heard!

A First Glimpse of Wuchang 234

— Xiao Mo

Just as Wuchang was beginning to have good fortune replacing Nanchang, I ran to Wuchang, and after staying in a small inn for only a day or two, Wuchang gave me a "coup de grâce"—that is, stuffy heat.

I had long heard rumors about the intense heat of Wuhan. How there is not a single breeze after the sun sets, how the streets are full of half-naked poor people at night, how the rich cannot sleep all night and have to hire a rickshaw to run around the streets until dawn, dozing off in the rickshaw.

At this time, it was only mid-spring. When I came, the willows of Nanjing had not yet sprouted, but the willows here already had an inch of new green. During the day, the wind stops, and it is strangely muggy, as if it were early summer weather. Many pedestrians on the street have already changed into lined or single clothes. I walked on the street for a while wearing woolen clothes and felt a head full of sweat. Although I grew up in the South and have traveled through the hottest places in the world, because of this first taste of the dry heat, I had to be wary of the future summer life in Wuchang.

Wuchang and Hankou—the Chicago of the East—are indeed separated by only a river, but this shallow water is enough to leave Wuchang in the ranks of medieval cities in many ways. Like the old large cities in the South, the streets of Wuchang, except for a few roads, are all paved with white stones, but new-style cars have recently been running on the narrow and uneven stone roads. When the horns of the cars sound from afar, pedestrians quickly move aside and stand on the side of the road, paying "attention to salute" to the cars. Only after the cars pass do they move forward. Although there are a few new-style houses, the old-style houses dominate. The dirty white walls, the black and swollen large doors, and the dark blue and gold-splattered screens inside exude the darkness and decadence of the Middle Ages. There are also black decorations in the shape of dragons and arrows on the lintels, which may be a symbol of the height of the family. Except for a few shops facing the road, the shelves and counters in the shops are all arranged in the old style. It is dark and gloomy inside, and except for the foreign goods stores, it is quiet all day long. When the lights are lit, neon lights can be seen on one or two prosperous streets, but most of the city—especially the residential areas—is hidden in darkness and silence. Only some handicraft workshops are still working at night under kerosene lamps, and some small grocery stores half-cover the doors, revealing the pitiful light. Soon, the sound of the night watchman's bamboo clapper also begins, completing the gloomy and lonely medieval atmosphere.

The scenery of Wuchang is naturally not bad. Mount Luojia, East Lake, South Lake, and other places have not yet been visited, so I dare not make a light review now, but the ten miles of tender yellow rapeseed flowers in the suburbs and the winding elegance of Baobing Park are already worth admiring. However, the famous Yellow Crane Tower is a bit vulgar. Climbing the stone steps to the end of Snake Mountain, one looks up and sees a gray building like a church bell tower, but the plaque in front reads "Yellow Crane Tower Historic Site," which is really unexpected. A few steps further ahead is the Aolüe Tower, which does have some momentum, but the surroundings are full of photo studios and fortune-telling stalls, the latter being even more numerous. Photography is originally a brand new novelty, but when it comes to China, it is associated with the Duke of Zhou, King Wen, and the arts of Ma Yi and Liu. Now that Wuchang has become the center of Chinese politics, it is also the main battlefield for pursuing fame and fortune. The business of the philosophers at the Yellow Crane Tower must be booming. When I entered the Lüzu Temple, someone was performing a ritual. A young woman was kneeling in front of the statue of the god, closing her eyes, and holding a piece of yellow paper in both hands. A Taoist nun and several Taoist priests were chanting scriptures while holding ritual instruments. In the corner of the hall, there was a niche dedicated to the reclining Lüzu, depicting the story of the Yellow Millet Dream. Next to the niche was a doorway with a cloth curtain hanging down. On the wall were the words "Restricted Area for Staff Only." Lifting the curtain, it turned out to be a telegraph office. Modern transportation has invaded the territory ruled by divine power. What a comical contradiction!

However, regardless of whether it is contradictory or mysterious, Wuchang is indeed having good luck. Just look at the sudden increase in people seeking advice on legal matters on the streets, the jingling sound of rickshaws is particularly loud, the rental advertisements for houses are posted and torn off as soon as they are put up, and several new restaurants have opened, and you will know. Ah! Wuchang is on the road to prosperity. Why it is prospering and how other places are doing, these questions will be answered by others. Please excuse me from writing any further.

Waiting for the Hare 235

— TK

Recent Thoughts 236

— Wei Zhongtian

Although I have had a better environment and a better mood to work hard and read some books in the past half year, I still feel that these days have been somewhat regrettable! When I wake up in the morning and see the sun shining in from the east window, it seems to flash by, and the day is over. When I see the sunset appearing from the west window, I watch the sunset hiding in the twilight with a feeling of regret, as if hope has disappeared so easily.

Although I have read quite a few books, I believe that if a person's knowledge comes entirely from books, it is limited. A young man who spends all day with a pen and a pile of books hiding in a room is not a happy thing. Knowledge should come from the lives of the broad masses, then it is rich and profound. What do you think, my friend?

In such good sunlight and good wind, I always feel that there is something more meaningful than reading waiting for me to do, waiting for me to experience, but I only hate that I lack that courage.

In the past, all hopes and all dreams were devoured by the demons of life. Today, the hope that has been reborn is very weak, as if feeling that I am too incompetent, too unpromising, and unworthy of doing anything. My great sorrow arises from this kind of self-reflection. Seeing others moving towards a great road day by day, while I am still standing on the line between darkness and light, how can I not be ashamed!

Watching spring go and then watching spring come again, spring is as good as ever, as young as ever, but my mood is getting older year by year. I am still young, but my heart is approaching old age. Thinking of this, I can't help but be startled. Where has the childlike innocence gone? Where has the enthusiasm of young people gone? It has turned into smoke and mist and been blown away by the great wind of life.

Since that surge of passion in my heart was taken away by autumn last year, I have been looking at the changes in everything in the world with a cold heart. How can I not want to rekindle this frozen emotion? However, life determines my will, so that I often think about it, but in the end I have to hide. One eye looks back at the old past, and the other eye looks far into the new future. In this situation, who can resist contradictions not lording over their heart? Who will not be led into a dark little room by contradictions?

Every spring, I inevitably feel a little homesick, and this year it seems to be even stronger. I haven't been back to my hometown for eight whole years. According to Chun Di's letter, my hometown is much thinner and calmer than it was eight years ago. In every alley, there are thin, long black hands reaching out to beg from passers-by. Strong young people have all flowed to the cities. Although my hometown is heading towards the line of death, there are still many things in my hometown that make me miss it. The longer I don't go home, the more I miss it. I think this is probably not just me.

In the spring of my hometown, the small mountain in front of my door is full of purple wildflowers. When I was a child, I would always pick ten or a hundred of them and put them in front of my bed, on my grandmother's lapel, and on myself. When they withered, I would go pick them again tomorrow. Anyway, spring doesn't leave, and the flowers can't be picked completely. Now, there are also purple flowers on the vase on my desk, but I don't have the childhood mood to put flowers on my lapel.

On "Scholars Despising Each Other" (3) 237

— Cao Juren

In the late Qing Dynasty, someone in Shanghai compiled a collection of essays by modern scholars into fifty volumes, and included Zhang Taiyan, Tan Fusheng, and Huang Gongdu. Zhang Taiyan wrote to Deng Shi, saying: "Tan and Huang are worthy of respect in terms of their aspirations and actions. However, their scholarship is sparse, and their writing lacks scrutiny. Although I am simple and crude, I dare not compare myself with them. Wang Renqiu, a modern scholar, can be said to have wandered in their field, but he still imitates their reputation and cannot go his own way; Kang Changsu often has good words, but they are somewhat cunning and unrestrained; I also do not want to be listed with these two worthies, and suggest that my humble essays be deleted to avoid being mixed in with them!" At that time, Liang Qichao's political essays were all the rage, and everyone was influenced by him, but Zhang Taiyan ridiculed him, saying: "Such as one or two elders, they are all talented in rhetoric and social interaction. They are scholars who seek fame and gain, and their writing is like blowing life into withered bones, not what is meant by being refined and substantial. Therefore, it is said: 'To make nothing into something, to make emptiness into fullness, to make simplicity into extravagance, it is difficult to be constant!'" Zhang Taiyan also looked down on Lin Shu and Yan Fu's translations, saying: "What the lower classes admire is Yan Fu and Lin Shu's kind! Although Fu's writing is meticulous, its style is like that of the imperial examination, as if it is pretending. Shu is even worse than Fu, his writing lacks selection, and his essence is mixed with impurities, and it is even infiltrated by the style of Tang Dynasty novels! He wants to imitate its style, but it is like dust covering it, like a decayed tooth smiling, like a curved shoulder walking, thinking it is beautiful, but only adding to its ugliness!" In this way, on the one hand, it is necessary to meet the needs of the times (Qichao said of himself: "At this time, I liberated myself and strived to be simple and clear, sometimes mixing in slang, rhymes, and foreign grammar, and I did not restrain myself in my writing. Scholars competed to imitate it, calling it the new literary style, while the elders hated it and ridiculed it as a wild fox; however, its writing was clear and methodical, and its writing often carried emotion, which had a kind of magic for readers."), on the other hand, it is necessary to have solid scholarship (Taiyan said of himself: "Those who imitate the arguments of the Tang and Song dynasties benefit from their eloquence, and those who imitate the arguments of the Han dynasty benefit from their memorization, which is enough: those who imitate the arguments of the Wei and Jin dynasties, do not merely adhere to the text above, and cannot defend themselves with words below, they must first prepare with learning."), and will never show mercy, expressing it in words and expressions.

Judging from this, truly, the literary world is like a battlefield. Since ancient times, there has never been a "peaceful" atmosphere. However, it is not a bad phenomenon in the literary world to set up formations from different standpoints and fight for three hundred rounds before sounding the gongs to withdraw the troops. Literature, both ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign, has progressed in this way. When Hugo's "Ernani" was staged at the Théâtre Français on the night of February 15, 1830, those classical writers sat upstairs and elsewhere, intending to obstruct the performance; on the other hand, romantic writers and young people who sympathized with them gathered in the main hall downstairs, preparing for the disturbance of the classical school. For a time, the theater seemed to have become a battlefield: but after this fierce struggle, Romanticism stepped into the French literary world. Looking at the events before us, the heated debate between the "Xinmin Congbao" and the "Min Bao" opened up a great situation since the Xinhai Revolution; the New Youth's charge launched the great tide of the May Fourth Movement; during the period of cultural advancement, great conflicts in the literary world were probably inevitable. If "scholars despising each other" is really like what "my family's" Zihuan said, "each despises what the other excels at, with what they excel at," and is only a kind of "criticism," not a "personal attack," I think it should exist and will inevitably exist. Su Zizhan wrote to Emperor Shenzong: "Gentlemen are harmonious but not the same, while petty people are the same but not harmonious; harmony is like harmonious soup, while sameness is like Jishui. Therefore, Sun Bao said: Zhou Gong was a great sage, and Zhao Gong was a great worthy, but they still did not like each other, which is recorded in the classics, and neither was harmed. Wang Dao of Jin can be said to be a founding minister. Every time he spoke to guests, everyone present praised him, but Wang Shu was not happy, thinking that people were not Yao and Shun, so how could everything be perfect; Dao also restrained himself and thanked him." Do we hope that today's literary world will become a place where everyone breathes through the same nostril and lives a life of nodding and agreeing?

Therefore, I am not against "scholars despising each other"; I hope that the Chinese literary world can cultivate a healthy and powerful atmosphere of criticism! (End)

Mr. Juqing (12) 238

— Ke Ling

A piece of news said: The new order issued by the Education Bureau requires all private school teachers to take exams. The exam questions are very difficult, and they also require testing on the Three Principles of the People. Those who fail are not allowed to teach. In fact, this is a way to clean up private schools. The list of several local private school teachers has been fully opened and reported by the district primary schools.

Another piece of news said: The district office sent an official letter to the Public Security Bureau, saying that private schools were forcibly pulling students from schools, deliberately destroying education, disrupting public security, and delaying learning. Police will be sent immediately to seal them off...

In addition, there are many almost absurd horror stories that fly over every day like they have wings. Although Mr. Juqing has some doubts about them, he dares not disbelieve them. Even the most absurd news that he knows is a rumor, he dares not definitely deny it. He is worried all day long and completely bewildered by this rumor.

He has no time to take care of the problem of rectifying the academic style anymore.

For six or seven days in a row, Mr. Juqing was surrounded by a kind of bewilderment and fear.

The reality may not be as severe as the rumors, but the district primary schools will definitely not give up easily, he understands this. Think of a way to deal with it, but he doesn't have one—what power does he have to confront the school? It would be a good strategy to contact all the private school teachers in the town and cooperate to deal with it, and Mr. Juqing also thought of it; but his stubborn nature made him hesitate: to get involved with those disreputable teachers? Although Mr. Juqing's current situation is a bit downcast, he still has a body of pride!

US President's Power Does Not Extend to the Sea 239

— Xiaomin

A dispatch from the National News Agency in Miami yesterday stated that President Roosevelt spent a day fishing on a yacht yesterday without catching a single fish. Today, he went to Consforden Island. An aide smiled and told the President that the President's power does not seem to extend to the sea. The aide's words are extremely funny and humorous. If power cannot reach the sea, let alone the two oceans.

The traditional policy of the United States is to manipulate world hegemony, but once the situation becomes urgent and uncontrollable, it immediately turns around and strictly adheres to neutrality, fearing involvement in the vortex of war. This is indeed a fishing trick of the Americans. Now that war clouds are permeating Europe and Asia, the United States has once again issued a special alert, fearing involvement in the vortex. From this point of view, the saying that the President's power does not extend to the sea is quite worthy of consideration.

In the past, novels said that Jiang Taigong met King Wen at the age of eighty. One day, Jiang Ziya was fishing on the bank of the Wei River. King Wen happened to pass by and ordered his attendants to ask him questions. Ziya said, "Big fish don't come, let small fish go." King Wen knew that this person must have a background, so he went to visit him in person. Their conversation was congenial, and he was overjoyed and said, "I have been looking forward to Taigong for a long time." Then he carried him back. Such a big fish was easily caught by Taigong.

It is also said that King Wen also liked to fish, but his fishing hook was not curved, but straight. His intention was that those who were willing would take the bait, and those who were unwilling would not be forced. I ask, which fish would be willing to be hooked? This kind of hypocritical means of selling benevolence and seeking fame naturally had another purpose. This kind of fishing method was to win the hearts of the people.

Now, the President of the United States has been fishing and fishing, fishing for a whole day, but has not caught a single fish. It seems that in the current trend, the United States' manipulative policies have not yet found a suitable opportunity.

Afu Restaurant 240

— Hua Zhi

When the ship arrived at the pier, a sign hanging under the eaves of the police亭子"Afu Restaurant" caught my attention. Because there was no hotel in the small town, and the ship arrived at the pier at dusk, people going to Xicun had to travel at night, so the police station was set up like that. Following the crowd onto the pier, a short, stout fellow with a round face jumped out of Afu Restaurant and stopped everyone to his shop. - I hadn't been home for several years, and everything in my hometown felt unfamiliar to me; I混进the restaurant inexplicably. The formerly small bedroom now had three tables placed in it, and ten or so people sat full like bees, and the stout fellow busied himself pouring tea and handing out towels; asking each guest what dishes they wanted to eat.

I sat in the corner as if in a dream. Although this was my hometown, everything was a strange sight after the ship arrived at the pier. Because I was not used to traveling by boat, it seemed like something was surging up in my stomach. When the stout fellow asked me what dishes I wanted to eat, I was stunned. - It wasn't that I couldn't think of the name of a dish, or that I simply didn't want to eat; wasn't this shop owner the policeman who used to wear a black uniform? He had been to Xicun because of a robbery on the road; that short stature, round face, the flesh on his cheeks piled his eyes into a line, a Maitreya Buddha-like forever smiling face!

"Are you going to Xicun, sir?"

I wanted to answer him that I was the son of Lu Xiangshin from Xicun, but did I look like someone from the village? Everyone who landed from this pier was from Xicun, and you could tell by listening to their Xitou accent. I couldn't speak the language of my hometown, and I was wearing an awkward outfit, so Afu, who was now a restaurant owner, or he looked at me with the eyes of a policeman.

"Are you called Afu?"

"Yes. What dishes would you like to eat, sir?"

"Why is this police station closed?"

"Are you from Xicun, sir?" Afu was surprised, and even those fellow villagers I didn't recognize gave me strange looks. "It's been closed for a long time. - Since Lu Xiangshin passed away, Xicun seems to have no master. No one is willing to掏腰包for the轮派police donation. Mrs. Lu paid for several months alone... The young master has been out for so long, and there is no news of 一佃. In this day and age, doing good deeds doesn't have a good ending!"

The people eating all started talking at once. My face turned red, and I couldn't say a word for a long time. I had been drifting outside alone for more than ten years, and my hometown had become like this: my father had died without me knowing, and my mother was probably looking forward to her son's return day and night?

"How is Mrs. Lu doing now?"

"Do you know her family, sir? Are you going to Xicun now?"

"Yes. - I am her son!"

Everyone gathered around, looking at me, and the restaurant was silent for a moment, as if the air was too tight for them to open their mouths. But I knew that this was an expression of their excessive affection, they were glad that the father of the good man had not died out!

But what could I do to repay their deep affection? I had been away for more than ten years, and my mother was living in difficulty. Could my own battle-scarred heart be thrown into a warm embrace again?

I looked迷惘ly at the dim kerosene lamp, and everything in front of me gradually blurred, and finally I could no longer see this unfamiliar hometown!

The Third Wife of the Eldest Son 241

— Yafei

Speaking of the Third Wife of the Eldest Son, her height is not taller than anyone else, but people偏生 call her the Third Wife of the Eldest Son. If, according to most people's opinions, say that she is shrinking now, that sentence can't be fully trusted; because when I was seven or eight years old, she was still a very robust middle-aged woman, at that time she didn't look much taller than she is now. If the "Eldest Son" refers to her husband - the Eldest Son's Grandfather - then maybe there's still some reason. However, the Eldest Son's Grandfather had already passed away when I was born, so how long he was, I never saw him.

It is said that the Third Wife of the Eldest Son died her husband when she was twenty-six years old, and although she has been a young widow until now, she is in her sixties, but she is very healthy. I have never heard her have a severe illness from childhood to now. A head of hair that is as black and shiny as oil, and a mouth full of snow-white and neat teeth, makes people doubt that she is only forty or fifty years old!

She doesn't have a biological son or daughter, but she inherited a nephew from the second room; but she never takes care of their affairs, only cooks and eats for herself. Usually, she always sits at home chanting Buddha or sticking ingots, and then goes to sell the ingots to every household in the village, earning some money to subsidize her expenses. When she is free, she might go for a walk in the few pieces of mountain land she proposed, looking at the flowers, fruits, and trees.

The Third Wife of the Eldest Son is 清潔 in love, and her relationship with people is also strangely good. No one in the village before or after will have a grudge against her. What she hates most is being a "Buddha's head" and sitting up at night, so she has never been a "Buddha's head" in her life, or sat up at night in a temple. She doesn't object to burning incense, but she doesn't want to go to Hangzhou and Putuo. She always burns incense in nearby places, and sometimes burns incense in the atrium of her own home, and counts it as done after kowtowing a few times. She said: "A thousand Buddhas and ten thousand Buddhas are just one Buddha. Burning incense doesn't matter whether it's far or near, just be sincere. Why rush to borrow the Buddha's name to游山玩景 after traveling a thousand and eight hundred miles?"

Her adopted daughter-in-law and she don't get along very well. This差儿 is of course her daughter-in-law's fault; being gluttonous and lazy doesn't count, doesn't she also secretly come to偸 her things, and even结掇the勇人得妈 has not heard a sound from his mouth for a long time. But she doesn't bother to argue about these things; because she understands that they inherited from her, but 看相 her share of the inheritance, and are not biological flesh and blood. She thinks: anyway, the inheritance will always be given to them sooner or later, so I决不好take it to the coffin with me, now it's better to be泰气and do a favor to others, and save myself a lot of trouble.

Recently, on the two beams of the main hall of her house, there is already a small plaque with the words "Pine and Cypress are Equally Chaste" in vermilion paint; that plaque was given to her by several绅董s of the entire district, and it is said that they also advanced a birth position for her in the 石公山节烈祠, this is considered a "glorious harvest" in exchange for her youth and happiness for her entire life!

Scattered Notes on Returning South 242

— Tianqi

The hearts of people returning home are probably very anxious. On the night I arrived in Songshi, I heard that the county-Song Highway had been opened to traffic, and that there was a bus at seven o'clock in the morning, which was a pleasant surprise. If I were to travel as usual, the water journey from Songshi to the county seat would take at least two full days to complete; now it can be shortened to within three hours, which is such a light and easy thing. Although it will cost a little more fare, I feel it is worth it.

The sky was not yet碧白 when the servant came to call at the door, saying that there were few buses and many people, so we had to go to the station two hours early. So, I hastily finished breakfast and set off immediately. Songshi was originally a small market town, and after walking through a small street and turning into an alley, you were in the countryside. At this time, the dim night shadows笼网d the earth, and the mountain shadows around were looming; the Venus was dragging its residual light high on the peak of 玉指. Walking past people's doors, I provoked a burst of dog barking. Now that I was close to home, hearing this亲切 dog barking, I couldn't help but feel an inexplicable comfort in my heart.

When I arrived at the station, it was indeed crowded with a团人. There were still two hours before the bus departure time, so I had to stand aside and wait patiently. But while seeing this situation, I couldn't help but hesitate, there were only two buses. There were so many people, and if I couldn't squeeze onto the bus, it would be too late to transfer to a墟boat, and I would have to stay in Songshi for another night, which would be terrible.

Finally, after struggling until dawn, the buses slowly drove out of the garage. The situation at this time was indescribably chaotic, to say the least. The front was already overcrowded, and the back was desperately surging forward; I was caught in the middle, and there was simply no room to maneuver. Fortunately, the shop servant desperately rushed forward, climbed in through the bus window, and grabbed a seat.

At this time, I had just calmed down, and the bus was also preparing to depart. At this moment, two soldiers with刺刀s inserted on their guns suddenly came over, aggressively slapped the front of the bus:

—Cannot depart!

The power of this "cannot depart" was like a bolt from the blue, shocking the passengers in the bus to look at each other in silence. Although I am a sojourner returning from another place, seeing this situation, I can understand eight or nine points of what is going on. But the driver unexpectedly raised a protest:

—Your company did not notify us in advance

—丢那妈! What if there was no notification? I'll watch you drive!

—We are doing things according to reason...

With a snap, a slap had already been pasted on the driver's mouth? Another soldier grabbed the driver's arm and pulled him out, and he had already fallen on the road with his feet in the air.

—丢那妈! Watch me shoot you, you bandit!

The soldier held the gun over and made a gesture of firing, but at this time the passengers shouted out involuntarily:

—Cannot!

—Cannot!

After a brief commotion, the soldier's gun didn't fire, but the bus still couldn't depart, and the driver, whose face was as swollen as a pumpkin from being hit, was also taken to the company.

The next day, I finally gave up on the idea of taking the bus and endured two days of困闷 water journey before arriving at the county seat.

Night Escape 243

— Yonghui

Thirty people in a team—and I was one of them—trying our best to make our footsteps as quiet as possible; not even our breathing was allowed to be heavy. This wasn't because we were paranoid or suspicious; it was real: if we didn't do this, we would immediately fall into the enemy's tight encirclement! We would become prisoners! We would be beheaded! We knew: the enemy was extremely cruel to us.

A moon like the light of a sesame oil lamp shone out from the dark gray clouds; on the yellow dirt road without reeds, the lines of the road could still be faintly distinguished: but we couldn't take the relatively smooth main road, we had to walk on the small road full of reeds. In order to avoid unexpected dangers, our palms were almost becoming feet crawling on the ground.

The small road was bumpy and full of potholes, and sharp stones that pierced the soles of our shoes were scattered all over it, and even more, gusts of numbness shot up our legs! We felt cold on our bodies, and our feet became even more slippery. We walked from 7 PM to 1 AM after midnight. I think we walked at most fifteen li (7.5 km): but both feet

Page 22

were twisted and sore.

The reed path was finally finished at 2 AM. Immediately following the end of the reed path, what unfolded before us was a fairly wide river; the silvery-white river water, under the dim moonlight, in the still night, was exceptionally beautiful and poetic; however, we didn't have the leisure to appreciate these things in this still and dangerous situation. My ears were occupied by the high-speed trembling of everyone's heart. Bending our waists to ninety degrees, we ran as nimbly as monkeys at the edge of the shallow grass: we had approached an extremely dangerous, life-or-death situation! Whether we could continue to live depended on whether we could cross this river tonight! Because according to the reports from the scouts: the enemy had already stationed themselves in the small village on the other side of the river.

A pontoon bridge approached us in a flurry of urgent running! Our hands all gripped our guns, ready to engage in hand-to-hand combat with the enemy if necessary! A bloody battle!

"Password!" A voice came from the dense forest on the other side of the river. I believe the hearts of all thirty of us jumped into our throats.

We rushed forward without a word! Trying to find a way out of the dead end! "Password!" The second voice was even more urgent!

"Password!" The third time it was issued, still without a response, the sentry fired a shot with a "bang."

Our volley of shots fired over, and the sentry's gunshot was silent. We rushed over like madmen!

But in the faint moonlight, the body of the sentry lying across the path was actually one of our own people. This could be seen from the markings on the clothes, even in the dim moonlight.

A chaotic sound of footsteps poured out from the foot of the mountain on the opposite side. We knew: they were probably coming to help after hearing the sentry's gunshot and our volley. To avoid misunderstanding, we shouted the secret signal to them loudly.

Opening section "Surprise"

The sky is pale, the clouds are clear, and the breeze is refreshing. A few lines of new geese pass through the sky. The busy waiter Gao Lishi is in the imperial garden, sweeping and tidying up. The autumn scenery in the inner garden is boundless. Everywhere there are ponds with water chestnuts and lotuses. After a short while, it is reported that Emperor Ming has arrived. Consort Yang, favored by him, is supported on either side. Countless osmanthus flowers are fragrant. Sometimes parrots call to each other. The imperial banquet is laid out on the flower pavilion. The table is full of delicacies from the sea and mountains. Consort Yang held a golden pot in her jade hands, the Emperor tapped the clapper, the Consort sang a song, and the dance of the Rainbow Skirt and Feather Coat was unparalleled in the world. Taizhen knelt down and offered three cups of wine. The Emperor happily helped her up. Consort Yang fell drunk on the Consort Yang couch. A picture of a begonia in spring sleep. Seeing the drunken bear, his appearance was bewitched. Who knew that the joy was not over, and the sorrow had already arrived. It was said that An Lushan had rebelled and returned to war. Approaching the capital, what could be done? The Tang dynasty had been at peace for a long time. The civil and military officials were unable to resist the enemy. Quickly order the six armies to protect the Emperor. The carriages and horses hurriedly traveled a long journey. Temporarily avoiding the smoke of war, they were fortunate enough to go to Shu. The poor weak woman, like a flower, shattered into jade and disappeared into a piece of silk. She was given death at Maweipo in a short time.

Classical Prose 246

Wang Bingmei, Donglai Boyi

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Marquis Jin of Quwo Annexes Jin (Continued)

From ancient times, the methods relied upon by sages to prevent disputes for ten thousand generations have all been destroyed. Later kings began to realize that humans can overcome heaven, and that it is possible to seize the heirship; that the young can bully the old; the disasters of usurpation are frequently seen in historical records. Those who brought China into the realm of barbarians were perhaps initiated by Jin and Zhou. Alas, to be noble beyond compare, to be rich beyond compare, the number of those who covet and desire it is numerous. If a brave person guards it with his heart, it will be taken away by someone twice as brave. If a wise person guards it, it will be taken away by someone even wiser. Guarding with oaths, they will sometimes be broken; guarding with laws, they will sometimes be abolished; guarding with city walls, they will sometimes be destroyed; guarding with armor and weapons, they will sometimes be defeated. Only by guarding it with heaven will people dare not compete with it. This is what those who possess the state rely on: that the fixed distinction between嫡庶 legitimate and illegitimate sons, eldest and youngest, comes from heaven. To disrupt the fixed distinction of heaven without reason is to destroy one's own reliance. Alas, how dangerous!

Shenbao Local Supplement, Film Special Issue

The Production of Mickey Mouse Cartoons at the Walt Disney Studios 248

— Huang Yingdai

The Mickey Mouse cartoons that we see on the screen last for ten minutes, but in the studio, it takes eight weeks to make them.

The first step in producing a Mickey Mouse cartoon is to decide on the story. Usually—but not always—Walt Disney comes up with the idea, preparing what kind of adventure Mickey Mouse will have in the new film. After the idea is there, a meeting is held with 25 or 30 employees of the Walt Disney Studios to decide on the story. After the outline of the story is planned, the humorist, Mike, gets to work deciding how Mickey Mouse should move in each scene of the story, and trying to insert as much funny and humorous material as possible.

The second step is a troublesome painting process. Humorous scenes and important dialogues must be drawn one by one.

An ordinary short film requires 9,000 to 10,000 paintings to be photographed, and each painting is done by hand. Each one is photographed on film, so you can imagine how heavy the workload is.

Walt Disney believes that sound should not only be added, but also be in sync with Mickey Mouse's movements. The movement of each step should be in harmony with each musical note. Therefore, in addition to painting, the second important task is composing the music. This work is done after the story is written, but before the painting begins. We can imagine that if the music is in eleven beats, then Mickey Mouse should take eleven steps on the screen. So, the music must be composed first, and then the painting can begin.

There is a design leader, like a director in an ordinary film company, who carefully directs the work of each artist based on the music and the anecdotes in the story, from the time Mickey Mouse enters the scene to the time he leaves the scene, how he should move.

This leader makes each segment of the film in harmony with the music. Generally, he has to edit 9,000 paintings, and each painting has to be drawn by the artist.

The film is transferred to film, and what about the background? Sometimes one hundred or more paintings are almost the same. So, these films do not need to be painted every time, they just need to be re-photographed. After the film is painted and the photography is completed, the second step is to add sound.

In a sound mixing room, the sound is recorded. There is a small orchestra sitting in the corner, and across from them is a glass room. The orchestra starts in this glass room under the direction of the conductor to test it once.

Inside the sound mixing room, there is a long table, almost as long as the room, and it is full of equipment. Four or five people are standing in front of the table, and there is a radio. In front of the orchestra, there are several smaller radios. These people are all music experts, and they can make each note play with unexpected excitement.

When the Mickey Mouse cartoon is finished in the Walt Disney Studios, the pictures are photographed on one film, and the sound is on another. Then they are put together. This work is relatively simple, and every film company can do it. After everything is finished, it is decided how many copies to print.

Humorous cartoons were not invented by Walt Disney. In 1928, when the sudden invention of talking films with sound and dialogue almost caused the entire film industry to collapse, cartoons were already not new things.

In the early part of 1928, Walt Disney imagined using a mouse as the main character in the film. At first, he named the mouse Mortimer Mouse, but later changed it to Mickey, entirely for the sake of brevity. Rabbits and other animals on cards had already met us. Mickey Mouse's appearance on the screen was just expanding a family of animals.

In the spring of the same year, Walt Disney had another idea, deciding to add music to Mickey Mouse's movements. The result was a success, and this was a new invention.

Walt Disney initially sold his films to several large film companies, until he later met someone in New York who gave him economic assistance to become independent. When his film was publicly screened in a small theater in mid-September, it received great praise from the New York audience, and from then on, Mickey Mouse cartoons occupied an important position.

Film Reviews

Review of "Border Town" 249

— Zhong Fei

Border Town—Grand Light

Paul Muni, who achieved extremely high acting achievements in works such as "The Story of Louis Pasteur" and "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang", but was not very commendable in "The Good Earth", has given people a deep impression and a good feeling. Therefore, this "Border Town" has also aroused great attention from the audience. In the current era of the star-centered system, people often take the leading actor as the goal to speculate on the quality of a certain film. On the one hand, because the actors give the audience the most direct attention, and on the other hand, the name of the leading actor is sometimes written larger than the title of the film on the film's billboard.

However, deciding the quality of a film based on the actor is by no means reasonable. It is true that film is a comprehensive art, and the acting skills of the stars occupy one of the important parts of the film's composition, but when the director and screenwriter, especially the script, cannot lay the foundation for the success of the work, even a genius actor can only be powerless. Paul Muni's failure in "The Good Earth" is a clear example. Which actor can achieve great success in a mediocre script? Therefore, regarding the evaluation of "Border Town", we cannot only base it on the acting skills of the leading actor, but rather the review of the content of the play is our most important task.

Looking at the story of this film, the playwright has a strong sense of justice, and his considerable degree of anger at the current society is very clearly expressed. In the male protagonist who was born humble, he expresses his dissatisfaction with society. He demands justice from society, no, he has even greater aspirations to demand justice from society on behalf of his group. Therefore, after graduating from a simple higher law school after five years, he immediately hung up his lawyer's sign with the money his mother exchanged for her ring. He was full of Lincoln's spirit to protect the human rights of the poor. However, the first time he practiced, he deeply believed that his ideals had failed (A rich woman drove her car and injured a poor old man, and as a result, she only paid a compensation fee of twenty-five yuan. He was also disqualified from being a lawyer.) He asserted. There is no justice or fairness in the current society, only money and power can become the victors. Up to this point, the playwright's anger is fully expressed. But where is the theme of the play? The playwright cannot instruct this young man with a sense of justice to engage in practical and effective struggles, but rather the individualism of trying to gain money and power in order to take revenge on society. We do not deny the existence of this kind of character. Young people with a sense of justice, if they cannot take the path of collectivism, then there is only individualistic revenge. However, when they are tempered again in the cruel reality, when their last hope is also disillusioned, they will inevitably realize it and turn from the wrong path of individualism to a positive path. However, the playwright is confused by the old worldview, and his understanding of reality cannot be observed correctly; when the male protagonist in his pen understands the existence of class after gaining money (he proposed to a rich woman, but the woman refused his request due to the disparity in class), he passively converted to the belief in God. This fully expresses the playwright's cowardice from active to passive, and at the same time serves as educational significance. And it gives the audience an impression.

Here, the merits and demerits of this film have already been judged. All that can be said is about technical aspects. From Paul Muni's makeup (in order to dress up as a Mexican, he painted his face brown, while also highlighting the whiteness and power of his eyes), you can tell that he is very talented and very serious. He vividly expresses the steadfast and intelligent personality of the young man with a sense of justice that we can often see. However, the script makes it so that he has no major scenes to do, and as a result, he only gives people a level of devotion to the point of perfection. On the other hand, in terms of the female lead, the screenwriter and director have strengthened her inner description. When she killed her husband and could not get the love of her lover, which caused a terrifying change, Bette Davis's performance was quite successful. (However, the tense parts were probably reshot several times, so it jumped very violently.) This is where the director's delicate technique is expressed, and the success of this psychological description should be the most important technical achievement of this film.

Commentary on "Cops Are Afraid of Their Wives" 250

— Hua Lun

“It’s　a　Cop”—Screening in Greater Shanghai

First, it must be said that the translated title "Cops Are Afraid of Their Wives" is too "business-minded" and somewhat unsuitable for the entire content of the play. This is because although the cop, the protagonist depicted in the play, is somewhat afraid of his wife, the playwright mainly wants to use the unfortunate experience of a relatively good cop to deliver a sermon that goes something like, "Good kids, work hard with all your might, it doesn't matter if you suffer a little hardship in body and mind, you can get promoted and make a fortune by relying on this." However, at the same time, for the sake of business, the author had to painstakingly cater to the audience with extremely low-level tastes. As a result, amidst the ridiculous gimmicks, the audience's burst of laughter drowned out the author's original intent of the sermon. On the contrary, the scene of the cop's promotion after enduring many foolish hardships also became a laughable ending.

The plot unfolds as the cop, Shi Bolai, is ordered to monitor a group of bandits who are stealing important secret formulas from a certain factory. Instead, he is seduced by the female bandit, Bao Baidi, and lets the bandits go. As a result, he is dismissed from the police force and falls into a pitiful and ridiculous situation of being scolded by his wife. Later, due to a coincidental coincidence, he tracks down the group of bandits again, and is once again seduced, leading to all sorts of ridiculous and embarrassing events. In the end, another coincidence occurs, finally enabling this cop, who has suffered greatly, to solve the case and achieve fame and fortune.

Such an empty story, coupled with several accidental coincidences and other shortcomings in the script, naturally feels unremarkable. However, due to the awkward face, exaggerated mannerisms, and ridiculous encounters of the lead actor, Xue Ni Huawade, the audience can indeed derive a lot of amusement.

The director, Maclean Rogers, has many clever touches. Hoder's performance is consistently exaggerated from beginning to end, with a sneaky and muddled tone, and a sense of affectation in everything from pronunciation to action. Naturally, this is a common problem in this type of film and for this type of character, but comparatively speaking, Howard has been quite successful here.

The entire play places excessive emphasis on the role of the cop played by Howard, and as a result, the entire play's mood and tone develop abnormally. In terms of acting skills, apart from the skating techniques in the two skating scenes being quite impressive, there is not much room for the supporting actors to show their skills.

Film Novel

Amateur Reporter (After Office Hours) (7) 252

— Tong Yun

Pengniside grabbed Zhuliya's collar and said, "You're crazy." Zhuliya said, "That's right, I'm crazy. It's all your fault." She fiercely beat Pengniside, shouting, "Let go! I'm going to reason with Xuelun. After I tell her about our relationship, let's see if she still wants you!" Pengniside held her back, and his anger became uncontrollable when he heard her words. He said, "You want to tell her?" Zhuliya was still struggling hard. Pengniside grabbed her throat with both hands. Zhuliya initially widened her eyes and struggled for a while, but soon lowered her head and stopped moving.

Pengniside laid Zhuliya on the ground, muttering curses, "You still want to tell her, huh!" Soon, he walked into the house with many pieces of wood in his hand. He saw Xuelun was on the phone. She held the phone and said, "Mr. Bolang Que? This is Xuelun Na Ge Tuo. I'm telling you, I can't do it anymore. I really don't have time to write that Riverside Association news. It's best if you write it yourself."

After she finished speaking, she hung up the phone and said to Pengniside. "Let's go. Let's go out for a walk. I'm hungry. Let's find a food cart and eat some pig intestines." Pengniside was not in the mood to keep her, so he accompanied her outside and got into his car. Pengniside accelerated and drove straight ahead. Xuelun was in the car, and for a moment she thought of Jiemu Bolang Que, wishing he could hear Pengniside's declarations of love to her, so he would know that she wasn't some excellent melon, and that she truly loved him from head to toe. As she was deep in thought, she suddenly saw a food cart parked by the side of the road and called for Pengniside to brake. She said, "We can eat some ham and eggs."

Pengniside didn't want to stop at first, but because Xuelun insisted, he had to stop. As they were eating ham and eggs at the food cart, the cart was equipped with a wireless radio. The radio constantly broadcasted calls from the police station. At this time, the radio suddenly shouted, "Police car number forty-seven…go to one thousand and one Sipailusi Street…domestic dispute…" Then it shouted again, "All police cars…rush to number sixty-two Aiwen Niu Road…rush…rush…"

Pengniside's heart was pounding, and he didn't know if his own case had been discovered, or if the radio would also shout it out. After Xuelun finished eating the ham and eggs, he quickly threw the money on the counter and pulled Xuelun away. Xuelun asked strangely. "What's wrong? What's your hurry?"

Early the next morning, Jiemu Bolang Que ran to Na Ge Tuo's house. He told Xuelun that Zhuliya Bode Sen had been murdered, and he wanted her to find a way to take him to the Bode Sen's house. He said, "This case is very bizarre, and it happened after the first night of the Riverside Association last night. There are many rumors circulating outside, and I don't know whose name will be implicated, so much so that it will be published in the newspaper. If I am at the Bode Sen's house, I can try to prevent them from involving your name."

When Xuelun heard his words, she thought they made sense, so she agreed to him, and tried her best to pretend to be indifferent and thanked him. Soon, they had arrived at the Bode Sen's house. In the hallway, they heard plainclothes detectives questioning the Bode Sen's servants. The servants all said that their master seemed to be in a bad mood when he returned from the Riverside Association last night because he had drunk some wine. One of the maids also said that the master and mistress had argued the night before. Pengniside's name was also frequently mentioned in the servants' mouths. They also said that Henry Bode Sen had once beaten his wife. (To be continued)
